<p><b>Brian Harold May</b>, <span style="font-size:85%;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (born 19 July 1947) is an English musician, singer, songwriter and astrophysicist who achieved international fame as the lead guitarist of the rock band <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>. He uses a home-built electric guitar, called the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>. His compositions for the band include "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Bottomed_Girls" title="Fat Bottomed Girls">Fat Bottomed Girls</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flash_(Queen_song)" title="Flash (Queen song)">Flash</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>".</p>
<p>He was appointed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Most_Excellent_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) in 2005 for "services to the music industry and for charity work".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> May attained a PhD in <a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">astrophysics</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_College" title="Imperial College">Imperial College</a> in 2007 and was <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Liverpool_John_Moores_University" title="Chancellor of Liverpool John Moores University">Chancellor of Liverpool John Moores University</a> from 2008 to 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> He has homes in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windlesham" title="Windlesham">Windlesham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> He is an active animal rights advocate and was appointed a vice-president of animal welfare charity the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RSPCA" title="RSPCA">RSPCA</a> in September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, a <a href="/wiki/Planet_Rock_(radio_station)" title="Planet Rock (radio station)">Planet Rock</a> poll saw May voted the 7th greatest guitarist of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> He was ranked at No. 26 on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine's list of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_greatest_guitarists_of_all_time" title="Rolling Stone's 100 greatest guitarists of all time">100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, May was ranked the 2nd greatest guitarist of all time by a <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_World" title="Guitar World">Guitar World</a></i> magazine readers poll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Brian Harold May, the only child of Harold and Ruth May, was born in <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_London" title="Hampton, London">Hampton, London</a> and attended the local Hampton Grammar School, then a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voluntary_aided" title="Voluntary aided">voluntary aided</a> school, (now <a href="/wiki/Independent_school" title="Independent school">independent</a> and known as <a href="/wiki/Hampton_School" title="Hampton School">Hampton School</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> He is of English and Scottish descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> During this time he formed his first band with vocalist and bassist <a href="/wiki/Tim_Staffell" title="Tim Staffell">Tim Staffell</a>, named 1984 after <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">novel of the same name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rcnov95_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-rcnov95-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> At Hampton Grammar School, he attained ten <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Education" title="General Certificate of Education">GCE</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O-Level" title="O-Level">Ordinary Levels</a> and three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-Level" title="A-Level">A-Levels</a> (Physics, Mathematics and Applied Mathematics).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rcnov95_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-rcnov95-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> He studied Mathematics and Physics at <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, graduating with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">BSc.</a> in Physics with honours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Musical career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1968.E2.80.931970:_Smile">1968–1970: Smile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1968–1970: Smile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile (band)</a></div>
<p>May formed the band <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile</a> in 1968. The group included <a href="/wiki/Tim_Staffell" title="Tim Staffell">Tim Staffell</a> as the lead singer and bassist, and later, drummer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a>, who also went on to play for <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>. The band lasted for only two years from 1968 to 1970, as Staffell left in 1970, leaving the band with a catalogue of nine songs. Smile would reunite for several songs on 22 December 1992. Taylor's band <a href="/wiki/The_Cross_(band)" title="The Cross (band)">The Cross</a> were headliners and he brought May and Staffell on to play "Earth" and "If I Were a Carpenter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> May also performed several other songs that night.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.931991:_Queen">1970–1991: Queen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970–1991: Queen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen (band)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hannover7907.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="600" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hannover7907.jpg/220px-Hannover7907.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hannover7907.jpg/330px-Hannover7907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hannover7907.jpg/440px-Hannover7907.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hannover7907.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May (right) on stage with Queen in 1979.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May also served as Queen's backing vocalist. In Queen's three-part vocal harmonies, May was generally the lower-range backing vocals. On some of his songs he sings the lead vocals, most notably the first verse of "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>", the final verse of "<a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven#.22Mother_Love.22" title="Made in Heaven">Mother Love</a>", the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_eight" title="Middle eight">middle eight</a> on "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>" and "Flash's Theme", and full lead vocals on "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Some_Day_One_Day" title="Some Day One Day">Some Day One Day</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack_(album)#She_Makes_Me_.28Stormtrooper_in_Stilettoes.29" title="Sheer Heart Attack (album)">She Makes Me (Stormtrooper in Stilettoes)</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">'39</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Company_(song)" title="Good Company (song)">Good Company</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_(album)#Long_Away" title="A Day at the Races (album)">Long Away</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_Dead,_All_Dead" title="All Dead, All Dead">All Dead, All Dead</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleeping_on_the_Sidewalk" title="Sleeping on the Sidewalk">Sleeping on the Sidewalk</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jazz_(Queen_album)#Leaving_Home_Ain.27t_Easy" title="Jazz (Queen album)">Leaving Home Ain't Easy</a>" and "Sail Away Sweet Sister".</p>
<p>Throughout Queen's career May frequently wrote songs for the band and has composed many worldwide hits "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Bottomed_Girls" title="Fat Bottomed Girls">Fat Bottomed Girls</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Who_Wants_To_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants To Live Forever">Who Wants To Live Forever</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>" as well as writing significant hit songs "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flash_(Queen_song)" title="Flash (Queen song)">Flash</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Now_I%27m_Here" title="Now I'm Here">Now I'm Here</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack#.22Brighton_Rock.22" title="Sheer Heart Attack">Brighton Rock</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Prophet%27s_Song" title="The Prophet's Song">The Prophet's Song</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Las_Palabras_de_Amor" title="Las Palabras de Amor">Las Palabras de Amor</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/No-One_But_You" title="No-One But You">No-One But You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">Save Me</a>". Typically, either <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> or May wrote the most songs on every Queen album.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brianrs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="558" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/170px-Brianrs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/255px-Brianrs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/340px-Brianrs.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brianrs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May playing his signature <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a> guitar, which contributed an essential part of Queen's sound.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the famous <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> concert in 1985, Mercury rang his band members and proposed writing a song together. The result was "<a href="/wiki/One_Vision" title="One Vision">One Vision</a>", which was basically May on music (the <i>Magic Years</i> documentary shows how he came up with the opening section and the basic guitar riff) and the lyrics were co-written by all four band members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For their 1989 release album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miracle_(album)" title="The Miracle (album)">The Miracle</a></i>, the band had decided that all of the tracks would be credited to the entire band, no matter who had been the main writer. Still, interviews and musical analyses tend to help identify the input of each member on each track. May composed "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>" for that album, as well as "<a href="/wiki/Scandal_(song)" title="Scandal (song)">Scandal</a>" (based on his personal problems with the British press). For the rest of the album he did not contribute so much creatively, although he helped in building the basis of "Party" and "Was It All Worth It" (both being predominantly Mercury's pieces) and created the guitar riff of "Chinese Torture".</p>
<p>Queen's subsequent album was <i><a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(album)" title="Innuendo (album)">Innuendo</a></i>, on which May's contributions increased, although more in arrangements than actual writing in most cases; for the <a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(song)" title="Innuendo (song)">title track</a> he did some of the arrangement for the heavy solo, then he added vocal harmonies to "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Going_Slightly_Mad" title="I'm Going Slightly Mad">I'm Going Slightly Mad</a>" and composed the solo of "<a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">These Are the Days of Our Lives</a>", a song for which the four of them decided the keyboard parts together. He changed the tempo and key of Mercury's song "The Hitman" and took it under his wing, even singing guide vocal in the demo. May also co-wrote some of the guitar lines in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bijou_(Queen_song)" title="Bijou (Queen song)">Bijou</a>".</p>
<p>Two songs that May had composed for his first solo album, "<a href="/wiki/Headlong_(song)" title="Headlong (song)">Headlong</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Live_With_You" title="I Can't Live With You">I Can't Live With You</a>", eventually ended up in the Queen project. His other composition was "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>", a group effort in which he was the coordinator and primary composer, but in which they all had input, Deacon and Taylor with the famous chord sequence. In recent years, he has supervised the remastering of Queen albums and various DVD and greatest hits releases. In 2004, he announced that he and drummer Roger Taylor were going on tour for the first time in 18 years as "Queen", along with <a href="/wiki/Free_(band)" title="Free (band)">Free</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bad_Company" title="Bad Company">Bad Company</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a>. Billed as "<a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a>", the band has played throughout 2005 and 2006 in South Africa, Europe, Aruba, Japan, and North America and released a new album with Paul Rodgers in 2008, entitled <i>The Cosmos Rocks</i>. This album was supported by a major tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1983.E2.80.931998:_the_Brian_May_band">1983–1998: the Brian May band</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1983–1998: the Brian May band">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="424" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg/170px-Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg/255px-Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg/340px-Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May playing his <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>, 1979</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During 1983, several members of Queen explored side projects. On 21 and 22 April in Los Angeles, May recorded his first solo work, a mini-album entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Fleet_Project" title="Star Fleet Project">Star Fleet Project</a></i>, on which he collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Van_Halen" title="Eddie Van Halen">Eddie Van Halen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> May contributed to former <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a> guitarist <a href="/wiki/Steve_Hackett" title="Steve Hackett">Steve Hackett</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Feedback_86" title="Feedback 86">Feedback 86</a></i>, playing guitar on the track "Cassandra" and providing guitar and vocals for "Slot Machine". "Slot Machine" was also co-written by May.</p>
<p>May worked with his second wife <a href="/wiki/Anita_Dobson" title="Anita Dobson">Anita Dobson</a> on her first album, in which she sang vocals to the <a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a> theme tune. In this form the tune became the song "<a href="/wiki/Anyone_Can_Fall_in_Love" title="Anyone Can Fall in Love">Anyone Can Fall in Love</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> May himself produced the song, which reached No. 4 in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> in August 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1989, May contributed guitar solos to the song "When Death Calls" on <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a> 14th album <i><a href="/wiki/Headless_Cross" title="Headless Cross">Headless Cross</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Living_in_a_Box" title="Living in a Box">Living in a Box</a> track "Blow The House Down" from the album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gatecrashing" title="Gatecrashing">Gatecrashing</a></i>.</p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"After the tragic break-up of any band, it feels impossible to continue but I was really glad that Brian did launch a solo career. He had such a lot of music in him and a great deal more to give"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —<a href="/wiki/Joe_Satriani" title="Joe Satriani">Joe Satriani</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Following the death of <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> in November 1991, May booked himself into a clinic in <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, and states; "I regarded myself as completely sick. I was wounded and very much in pieces. I went into a serious depression. I was subsumed by feelings of loss."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mail_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mail-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> He chose to deal with his grief by committing himself as fully as possible to work, first by finishing his solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Light" title="Back to the Light">Back to the Light</a></i>, and then touring worldwide to promote it. He frequently remarked in press interviews that this was the only form of self-prescribed therapy he could think of.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a> vocalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joe_Elliot" title="Joe Elliot">Joe Elliot</a>, "It was undoubtedly an enormous and terrible blow to lose someone he was so close to. Personally, I know it ripped the heart out of Brian, but having said that, he was in great spirits after the album was finished."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In late 1992, <a href="/wiki/The_Brian_May_Band" title="The Brian May Band">the Brian May Band</a> was officially formed. An early version of the band was loosely formed for 19 October 1991, the date of the band's last concert of reunion.October 1991, when May took part in the <i>Guitar Legends</i> guitar festival in <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, Spain. The line-up for his performance was May on vocals and lead guitar, <a href="/wiki/Cozy_Powell" title="Cozy Powell">Cozy Powell</a> on drums and percussion, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Moran_(music_producer)" title="Mike Moran (music producer)">Mike Moran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Wakeman" title="Rick Wakeman">Rick Wakeman</a> on keyboards, and <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Ryder" title="Maggie Ryder">Maggie Ryder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miriam_Stockley" title="Miriam Stockley">Miriam Stockley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Thompson_(English_musician)" title="Chris Thompson (English musician)">Chris Thompson</a> on backing vocals. The original line-up was May on vocals and lead guitar, Powell on drums and percussion, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Casswell" title="Michael Casswell">Michael Casswell</a> on guitar, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Murray_(British_musician)" title="Neil Murray (British musician)">Neil Murray</a> on bass, and Ryder, Stockley and Thompson on backing vocals. This version of the band lasted only during the South American support tour (supporting <a href="/wiki/The_B-52%27s" title="The B-52's">The B-52's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cocker" title="Joe Cocker">Joe Cocker</a>) on only five dates.</p>
<p>Afterwards, May made significant changes, feeling the group never quite gelled. May brought guitarist <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Moses" title="Jamie Moses">Jamie Moses</a> on board to replace Mike Caswell. The other change made was in the backing vocals department, when Ryder, Stockley and Thompson were replaced with <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Porter" title="Catherine Porter">Catherine Porter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shelley_Preston" title="Shelley Preston">Shelley Preston</a>. On 23 February 1993, this new line-up of The Brian May Band began its world tour in the US, both supporting <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a> and headlining a few dates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour would take them through North America, Europe (support act: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Robby_Valentine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Robby Valentine (page does not exist)">Valentine</a>) and Japan. After the tour ended on 18 December 1993, May returned to the studio with fellow surviving Queen band members <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Meddows-Taylor" title="Roger Meddows-Taylor">Roger Taylor</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">John Deacon</a> to work on tracks that became <i><a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven" title="Made in Heaven">Made in Heaven</a></i>, the final Queen studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buckley_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The band took Mercury's solo album demos and last recordings, which he managed to perform in the studio after the album <i><a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(album)" title="Innuendo (album)">Innuendo</a></i> was finished, and completed them with their additions both musically and vocally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Work on the album after Mercury's death originally began in 1992 by Deacon and May, but was left until a later date due to other commitments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buckley_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995, May began working towards a new solo album of covers tentatively named <i>Heroes</i>, in addition to working on various film and television projects and other collaborations. May subsequently changed the approach from covers to focus on those collaborations and on new material. The songs included <i><a href="/wiki/Another_World_(Brian_May_album)" title="Another World (Brian May album)">Another World</a></i>, and featured mainly <a href="/wiki/Spike_Edney" title="Spike Edney">Spike Edney</a>, Cozy Powell, Neil Murray and Jamie Moses. On 5 April 1998, Cozy Powell was killed in a car accident on the <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway" title="M4 motorway">M4 motorway</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, England. This caused a huge, unexpected disruption to the upcoming tour for The Brian May Band, with a new drummer being needed at short notice. <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ferrone" title="Steve Ferrone">Steve Ferrone</a> was brought on to help May finish recording drums and to join the band for the early stage promotional tour of five dates in Europe before the world tour. Following the early promotional tour, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Singer" title="Eric Singer">Eric Singer</a> replaced Steve Ferrone for the full 1998 world tour.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.E2.80.93present">2000–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="1224" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Brian_May.JPG/180px-Brian_May.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Brian_May.JPG/270px-Brian_May.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Brian_May.JPG/360px-Brian_May.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May performing in Chile, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From his last solo release in 1998 May has been performing as a solo artist, as part of an ensemble, and infrequently as Queen with <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a>. On 22 October 2000, Brian May made a guest appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="Motörhead">Motörhead</a> 25th Anniversary show at <a href="/wiki/Brixton_Academy" title="Brixton Academy">Brixton Academy</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Clarke" title="Eddie Clarke">Eddie Clarke</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="Motörhead">Motörhead</a> guitarist) for the encore song "<a href="/wiki/Overkill_(Mot%C3%B6rhead_song)" title="Overkill (Motörhead song)">Overkill</a>". In the Queen's birthday honours list of 2005, he was made a Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Order of the British Empire</a> "for services to the music industry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> May is a friend of singer and musician <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a> and was a special guest at the <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a> reunion concert at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a> in 2007. The two had worked together at the Prince's Trust Rock Gala in 1988.</p>
<p>May worked extensively with stage actress and singer <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Ellis" title="Kerry Ellis">Kerry Ellis</a> after he cast her in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You_(musical)" title="We Will Rock You (musical)">We Will Rock You</a></i>. He produced and arranged her debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Anthems_(Kerry_Ellis_album)" title="Anthems (Kerry Ellis album)">Anthems</a></i> (2010), a follow-up to her extended play <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_in_Rock" title="Wicked in Rock">Wicked in Rock</a></i> (2008), as well as appearing with Ellis at many public performances – playing guitar alongside her. He also contributed a guitar solo to <a href="/wiki/Meat_Loaf" title="Meat Loaf">Meat Loaf</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hang_Cool,_Teddy_Bear" title="Hang Cool, Teddy Bear">Hang Cool, Teddy Bear</a></i> album in exchange for the use of drummer <a href="/wiki/John_Miceli" title="John Miceli">John Miceli</a>. Along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elena_Vidal" title="Elena Vidal">Elena Vidal</a>, Brian May released a historical book in 2009 entitled <i><a href="/wiki/A_Village_Lost_and_Found" title="A Village Lost and Found">A Village Lost and Found: Scenes in Our Village</a></i>. The book is an annotated collection of stereoscopic photographs taken by the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> photographer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Richard_Williams" title="Thomas Richard Williams">T. R. Williams</a> and it is sold with a focussing stereoscope. May became an enthusiast of stereoscope photographs as a child, and first encountered the work of Williams during the late 1960s. In 2003 May announced a search to identify the actual location of the <i>Scenes in Our Village</i> images. In 2004 May reported that he had identified the location as the village of <a href="/wiki/Hinton_Waldrist" title="Hinton Waldrist">Hinton Waldrist</a> in Oxfordshire.</p>
<p>On 20 May 2009, May and Queen band mate Roger Taylor performed "We Are the Champions" live on the season finale of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> with winner <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a> and runner-up <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> providing a vocal duet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIdol_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIdol-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2009, May appeared with Taylor on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i>, with Queen mentoring the contestants, then later performing "Bohemian Rhapsody". In April 2010, May founded the "Save Me" 2010 project to work against any proposed repeal of the British fox-hunting ban, and also to promote animal rights in Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-save-me.org.uk_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-save-me.org.uk-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2011 it was announced that May would tour with <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Ellis" title="Kerry Ellis">Kerry Ellis</a>, playing 12 dates across the UK in May 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 March 2013 May and Ellis played a free thirty minute acoustic set at <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras railway station</a> to launch Tiger Track, a three-week tiger conservation event. Their set list included Queen's "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_Little_Thing_Called_Love" title="Crazy Little Thing Called Love">Crazy Little Thing Called Love</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 April 2011 <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> confirmed that May would play guitar on her track "<a href="/wiki/You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="You and I (Lady Gaga song)">You and I</a>" from her latest album <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way" title="Born This Way">Born This Way</a></i>, released on 23 May 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2011, May performed with <a href="/wiki/Tangerine_Dream" title="Tangerine Dream">Tangerine Dream</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Starmus_Festival" title="Starmus Festival">Starmus Festival</a> on <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, celebrating the 50th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a>'s first spaceflight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 August, May performed "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Black_Parade" title="Welcome to the Black Parade">Welcome to the Black Parade</a>" with American rock band <a href="/wiki/My_Chemical_Romance" title="My Chemical Romance">My Chemical Romance</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reading_Festival" title="Reading Festival">Reading Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> On 28 August, May performed "You and I" live with Lady Gaga at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a> at the Nokia Theatre, Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> On 10 October, May made an appearance to celebrate the reunion of British rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Darkness_(band)" title="The Darkness (band)">The Darkness</a> at an "intimate" <a href="/wiki/100_Club" title="100 Club">100 Club</a> show with support from <a href="/wiki/Dark_Stares" title="Dark Stares">Dark Stares</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Darkness_Wow_The_100_Club_At_Intimate_Show_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Darkness_Wow_The_100_Club_At_Intimate_Show-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Darkness_.40_100_Club_10_October_2011_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Darkness_.40_100_Club_10_October_2011-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> A long-time fan of the group, May performed three songs onstage with The Darkness, including Queen's "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", at the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a> on their subsequent "comeback" tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Guitarist_Brian_May_Joins_The_Darkness_On_Stage_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Guitarist_Brian_May_Joins_The_Darkness_On_Stage-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QUEEN.27s_BRIAN_MAY_Performs_With_THE_DARKNESS_In_London_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-QUEEN.27s_BRIAN_MAY_Performs_With_THE_DARKNESS_In_London-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Europe Music Awards">2011 MTV Europe Music Awards</a> on 6 November, Queen received the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award_for_Global_Icon" title="MTV Europe Music Award for Global Icon">Global Icon Award</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> presented to Brian May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen closed the awards ceremony, with <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> on vocals, performing "The Show Must Go On", "We Will Rock You" and "We Are the Champions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The collaboration garnered a positive response from both fans and critics, resulting in speculation about future projects together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen + Adam Lambert played two shows at the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a>, London on 11 and 12 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Both shows sold out within 24 hours of tickets going on open sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> A third London date was added for 14 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> On 30 June, Queen + Lambert performed in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, Ukraine at a joint concert with <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> for the Elena Pinchuk ANTIAIDS Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen also performed with Lambert on 3 July 2012 at Moscow's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow)">Olympic Stadium</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> and on 7 July 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Stadion_Miejski_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Stadion Miejski (Wrocław)">Municipal Stadium</a> in Wroclaw, Poland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, May featured on <a href="/wiki/N-Dubz" title="N-Dubz">N-Dubz</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Dappy" title="Dappy">Dappy</a>'s solo single "<a href="/wiki/Rockstar_(Dappy_song)" title="Rockstar (Dappy song)">Rockstar</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dappy_.27pays_tribute_to_Amy_Winehouse.27_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dappy_.27pays_tribute_to_Amy_Winehouse.27-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> providing "rumbling guitar riffs which culminate in an electrifying solo".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27Rockstar.27_-_Single_review_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27Rockstar.27_-_Single_review-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The pair also collaborated on a performance of "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_One" title="BBC Radio One">BBC Radio One</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Live_Lounge" title="Live Lounge">Live Lounge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dappy_Will_Rock_You_in_the_Live_Lounge_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dappy_Will_Rock_You_in_the_Live_Lounge-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 August 2012, Queen performed at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics2012_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics2012-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> May performed part of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_Rock_(song)" title="Brighton Rock (song)">Brighton Rock</a>" solo before being joined by Taylor and solo artist <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a> for a performance of "We Will Rock You".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics2012_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics2012-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> On 16 September 2012, May appeared at the Sunflower Jam charity concert at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, performing alongside bassist <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_(musician)" title="John Paul Jones (musician)">John Paul Jones</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>), drummer <a href="/wiki/Ian_Paice" title="Ian Paice">Ian Paice</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>), and vocalists <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">Bruce Dickinson</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Alice_Cooper" title="Alice Cooper">Alice Cooper</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> On 20 September 2013, Queen + Lambert performed at the <a href="/wiki/IHeartRadio_Music_Festival" title="IHeartRadio Music Festival">iHeartRadio Music Festival</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Hotel_%26_Casino" title="MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino">MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino</a> in Las Vegas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, May recorded the soundtrack for the British independent film <a href="/wiki/51_Degrees" title="51 Degrees">51 Degrees</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian_May.27s_IMDB_page_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brian_May.27s_IMDB_page-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> directed by German film director Grigorij Richters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian_May.27s_Official_Blog_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brian_May.27s_Official_Blog-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The film will premiere at the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Starmus_Festival" title="Starmus Festival">Starmus Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starmus_announces_51_Degrees_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starmus_announces_51_Degrees-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starmus_announces_Stephen_Hawking_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starmus_announces_Stephen_Hawking-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.932009:_Queen_.2B_Paul_Rodgers">2004–2009: Queen + Paul Rodgers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2004–2009: Queen + Paul Rodgers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="773" data-file-width="1024" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/220px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/330px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/440px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2005 <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of 2004, May and Taylor announced that they would reunite and return to touring in 2005, with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a> (founder and former lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Free_(band)" title="Free (band)">Free</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Company" title="Bad Company">Bad Company</a>). Brian May's website also stated that Rodgers would be "featured with" Queen as <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a>, not replacing the late Freddie Mercury. The retired John Deacon would not be participating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bmcom_jdr_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-bmcom_jdr-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2005 and 2006 Queen and Paul Rodgers embarked on a <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">world tour</a>, the first leg being Europe and the second, Japan and the US in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen2006_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen2006-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> On 25 May 2006, Queen received the inaugural <a href="/wiki/VH1_Rock_Honors" title="VH1 Rock Honors">VH1 Rock Honors</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay_Events_Center" title="Mandalay Bay Events Center">Mandalay Bay Events Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, Nevada, and May and Taylor were joined on stage with the <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a> to perform a selection of Queen songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen2006_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen2006-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 August 2006, May confirmed through his website and fan club that Queen + Paul Rodgers would begin producing their first studio album beginning in October, to be recorded at a "secret location".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cosmos_Rocks" title="The Cosmos Rocks">The Cosmos Rocks</a></i>, was released in Europe on 12 September 2008 and in the United States on 28 October 2008. Following the album the band again embarked on a tour through Europe and parts of the US, opening on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_Square,_Kharkiv" title="Freedom Square, Kharkiv">Kharkov's freedom square</a> in front of 350,000 Ukrainian fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kharkov_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kharkov-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The show in Ukraine was later <a href="/wiki/Live_in_Ukraine" title="Live in Ukraine">released on DVD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kharkov_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kharkov-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen and Paul Rodgers officially split up on 12 May 2009. Rodgers does not rule out the possibility of working together again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Highlights">Highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_2005_1010016.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="764" data-file-width="870" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Queen_2005_1010016.JPG/220px-Queen_2005_1010016.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Queen_2005_1010016.JPG/330px-Queen_2005_1010016.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Queen_2005_1010016.JPG/440px-Queen_2005_1010016.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_2005_1010016.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May performing in Frankfurt in 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brian May began composing in 1968 to 1969, and through the years he has collaborated with other songwriters, including Frank Musker, with whom he wrote "<a href="/wiki/Too_Much_Love_Will_Kill_You" title="Too Much Love Will Kill You">Too Much Love Will Kill You</a>", and with Elizabeth Lamers, whose music won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Award" title="Ivor Novello Award">Ivor Novello Award</a> for Best Song Musically &amp; Lyrically in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> A meticulous arranger, he focuses on multi-part harmonies, often more <a href="/wiki/Counterpoint" title="Counterpoint">contrapuntal</a> than parallel – a relative rarity for rock guitar. Examples are found in Queen's albums <i>A Night at the Opera</i> and <i>A Day at the Races</i>, where he arranged a jazz band for guitar mini-orchestra ("Good Company"), a vocal canon ("The Prophet's Song") and guitar and vocal counterpoints ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teo_Torriatte" title="Teo Torriatte">Teo Torriatte</a>").</p>
<p>May explored a wide variety of styles in guitar, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweep_picking" title="Sweep picking">sweep picking</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Was_It_All_Worth_It" title="Was It All Worth It">Was It All Worth It</a>", "Chinese Torture"), <a href="/wiki/Tremolo" title="Tremolo">tremolo</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_Rock_(song)#Brighton_Rock" title="Brighton Rock (song)">Brighton Rock</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Crazy" title="Stone Cold Crazy">Stone Cold Crazy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Death_on_Two_Legs_(Dedicated_to...)" title="Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)">Death on Two Legs</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_Lady" title="Sweet Lady">Sweet Lady</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Get_Down_Make_Love" title="Get Down Make Love">Get Down Make Love</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_Attack" title="Dragon Attack">Dragon Attack</a>"), <a href="/wiki/Tapping" title="Tapping">tapping</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bijou_(Queen_song)" title="Bijou (Queen song)">Bijou</a>", "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Late" title="It's Late">It's Late</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Resurrection" title="Resurrection">Resurrection</a>", "Cyborg", "Rain Must Fall", "Business", "China Belle", "I Was Born To Love You"), slide guitar ("Drowse", "Tie Your Mother Down"), <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Hendrix</a> sounding licks ("<a href="/wiki/Liar_(Queen_song)" title="Liar (Queen song)">Liar</a>", "Brighton Rock"), tape-delay ("Brighton Rock", "White Man") and melodic sequences ("<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Killer_Queen" title="Killer Queen">Killer Queen</a>", "<a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">These Are the Days of Our Lives</a>"). Some of his solos and orchestral parts were composed by <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, who then asked May to bring them to life ("Bicycle Race", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lazing_on_a_Sunday_Afternoon" title="Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon">Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon</a>", "Killer Queen", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Old_Fashioned_Lover_Boy" title="Good Old Fashioned Lover Boy">Good Old Fashioned Lover Boy</a>"). May also performed notable acoustic works, including the acoustic guitar live version of "<a href="/wiki/Love_of_My_Life_(Queen_song)" title="Love of My Life (Queen song)">Love of My Life</a>" from 1975's <i>A Night at the Opera</i>, the finger-picked solo of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Queen_(As_It_Began)" title="White Queen (As It Began)">White Queen</a>" and the <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a>-influenced "'39".</p>
<p>In January 2007, the readers of <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_World" title="Guitar World">Guitar World</a></i> voted May's guitar solos "Bohemian Rhapsody", "Brighton Rock" into the "top 50 Greatest Guitar Solos of all time" ("Bohemian Rhapsody" was voted No. 20 and "Brighton Rock" was voted #41).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Aided by the uniqueness of his guitar – the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a> – May was often able to create strange and unusual sound effects. For example, he was able to imitate an orchestra in the song "<a href="/wiki/Queen_II#Procession" title="Queen II">Procession</a>"; in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Get_Down,_Make_Love" title="Get Down, Make Love">Get Down, Make Love</a>" he was able to create various sound effects with his guitar; in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Company_(song)" title="Good Company (song)">Good Company</a>" he used his guitar to mimic a trombone, a piccolo and several other instruments for the song's Dixieland jazz band feel. Queen used a "No synthesizers were used on this album" sleeve note on their early albums to make this clear to the listeners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> May also used his guitar to create the chime effect in Bohemian Rhapsody.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bohrapchimes_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-bohrapchimes-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_instruments">Other instruments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other instruments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first instrument May learned to play was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banjolele" title="Banjolele">banjolele</a>, which he played on Queen's song "Bring Back That Leroy Brown" (live and in the studio). For "Good Company", he used a regular baritone ukulele which he had bought in Hawaii on a holiday. Occasionally, May would also record on other string instruments such as harp (one chord per take, then copied and pasted by the engineer to make it sound like a continuous performance) and bass (on some demos and many songs in his solo career, and the Queen + Paul Rodgers album).</p>
<p>As a child, he was also trained on classical piano. Although Freddie Mercury was the band's primary pianist, May would occasionally step in (such as on "<a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">Save Me</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flash_(Queen_song)" title="Flash (Queen song)">Flash</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Who_Wants_To_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants To Live Forever">Who Wants To Live Forever</a>"). From 1979 onwards, he also played synthesisers, organ ("Wedding March", "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Live" title="Let Me Live">Let Me Live</a>") and programmed drum-machines for both Queen and outside projects (such as producing other artists and his own solo records).</p>
<p>May is also an accomplished singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> From Queen's <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_II" title="Queen II">Queen II</a></i> to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Game_(Queen_album)" title="The Game (Queen album)">The Game</a></i>, May contributed lead vocals to at least one song per album. May co-composed a mini-opera with <a href="/wiki/Lee_Holdridge" title="Lee Holdridge">Lee Holdridge</a>, <i>Il Colosso</i>, for <a href="/wiki/Steve_Barron" title="Steve Barron">Steve Barron</a>'s 1996 film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Pinocchio_(1996_film)" title="The Adventures of Pinocchio (1996 film)">The Adventures of Pinocchio</a></i>. May performed the opera with <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hadley" title="Jerry Hadley">Jerry Hadley</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sissel_Kyrkjebo" title="Sissel Kyrkjebo">Sissel Kyrkjebo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Just_William" title="Just William">Just William</a>. On-screen, it was performed entirely by puppets.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicianship">Musicianship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Musicianship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="507" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg/170px-Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg/255px-Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg/340px-Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May <a href="/wiki/Tapping" title="Tapping">tapping</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"He's a class act from head to toe, and it shows in his playing. I can listen to any player and pantomime their sound, but I can't do Brian May. He's just walking on higher ground."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —<a href="/wiki/Steve_Vai" title="Steve Vai">Steve Vai</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Brian May has been referred to as a virtuoso guitarist by many publications and musicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutcliffe_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sutcliffe-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> He has featured in various music polls of great rock guitarists, and in 2011 was ranked number 26 on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine's list of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_greatest_guitarists_of_all_time" title="Rolling Stone's 100 greatest guitarists of all time">100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Van_Halen" title="Van Halen">Van Halen</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Hagar" title="Sammy Hagar">Sammy Hagar</a> stated, "I thought Queen were really innovative and made some great sounding records.. I like the rockin' stuff. I think Brian May has one of the great guitar tones on the planet, and I really, really love his guitar work."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutcliffe_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sutcliffe-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> May mainly used the "<a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>", which he designed when he was only 16 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rdspecial_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-rdspecial-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> It was built with wood from an 18th century fireplace. His comments on the guitar:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"I like a big neck – thick, flat and wide. I lacquered the fingerboard with Rustin's Plastic Coating. The tremolo is interesting in that the arm's made from an old bicycle saddle bag carrier, the knob at the end's off a knitting needle and the springs are valve springs from an old motorbike."</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">—Brian May<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</blockquote>
<p>In addition to using his home-made guitar he prefers to use coins (especially <a href="/wiki/Sixpence_(British_coin)" title="Sixpence (British coin)">a sixpence</a> from the farewell proof set of 1970), instead of a more traditional plastic <a href="/wiki/Plectrum" title="Plectrum">plectrum</a>, on the basis that their rigidity gives him more control in playing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> He is known to carry coins in his pockets specifically for this purpose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>May's early influences were <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard" title="Cliff Richard">Cliff Richard</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Shadows" title="The Shadows">the Shadows</a>, who he says were "the most metallic thing(s) out at the time." Many years later he gained his opportunity to play on separate occasions with both Cliff Richard and Shadows lead guitarist <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a>. He has collaborated with Cliff Richard on a re-recording of the Cliff Richard and The Shadows (then known as The Drifters) 1958 hit "<a href="/wiki/Move_It" title="Move It">Move It</a>" on the Cliff Richard duets album <i>Two's Company</i> which was released on 6 November 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Brian May always stated that <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a> were the greatest influences on him. On <i>Queen for an Hour</i> 1989 Interview on BBC Radio 1, May listed <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> as his guitar heroes. In a 1991 interview for <i>Guitar World magazine</i>, May referred to <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a> as "my inspiration", and on seeing <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a> stated, "We used to look at those guys and think, "That's the way it should be done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Influenced by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a>, May states; "I don't think anyone has epitomised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riff#Riff" title="Riff">riff</a> writing better than Jimmy Page – he's one of the great brains of rock music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the time in which May and his father were building the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>, May also produced plans to build a second guitar. However, so successful was the Red Special, that May had no need to build another guitar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Spade_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Spade-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> These plans were eventually given to guitar <a href="/wiki/Luthier" title="Luthier">luthier</a> Andrew Guyton in around 2004/05, some slight modifications were made and the guitar was built. It was named "The Spade", as the shape of the body resembled the form shown on playing cards. However the guitar also came to be known as "The Guitar That Time Forgot".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Spade_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Spade-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Guitars_and_keyboards">Guitars and keyboards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Guitars and keyboards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="1816" height="366" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png/220px-Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png/330px-Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png/440px-Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Red_special_before_and_after_restoration.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May's <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a> before (top) and after (bottom) restoration</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of May's electric guitar work live and in the studio was done on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>, which he built with his father, an electronics engineer, during his teenage years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1975 onwards, he has also had some replicas made, some of which were also used for live and recording purposes, others were mainly spares. The most famous replicas were made by John Birch (in 1975—May actually smashed it during a concert in the States in 1982), <a href="/wiki/Greco_guitars" title="Greco guitars">Greco</a> BM90 (featured in the promo video of "Good Old-Fashioned Lover Boy" in 1977), Guild (back-up from 1984 to 1993), Fryers (1997–1998, used both live and in the studio) and Guyton<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> (back-up from 2003 to present). On stage, May used to carry at least one back-up guitar (in case he broke a string) and occasionally would use others for certain songs or parts, such as alternate tunings. Currently, May owns a company which makes guitars whose design is modelled after the original Red Special guitar.</p>
<ul>
<li>July 1973 – May 1974: Fender Stratocaster Pre-CBS</li>
<li>October 1974 – May 1975: Gibson Les Paul Deluxe, and the Stratocaster from the previous tour.</li>
<li>November 1975 – May 1976: Same two guitars as before, plus a natural finish John Birch replica of the Red Special.</li>
<li>September 1976: Same three as before, plus a Martin D-18 acoustic for "'39".</li>
<li>January 1977 – August 1979: Just the Birch replica plus an Ovation Pacemaker 12-string acoustic on some numbers ("'39", "Love of My Life", "Dreamer's Ball").</li>
<li>November 1979 – June 1982: Birch replica (back-up), Fender Telecaster ("Crazy Little Thing Called Love" 2nd verse, middle-eight and solo), Ovation (acoustic numbers).</li>
<li>July – November 1982: Added a Gibson Flying V as second back-up. On 9 August 1982 Brian smashed the Birch guitar, so the Flying V became the only spare.</li>
<li>August – October 1984: The Flying V became a second back-up again as his main spare was the Guild replica. He also used Roger Taylor's Gibson Chet-Atkins Classical Electric.</li>
<li>July 1985 – August 1986: Gibson Flying V no longer used. The rest remained the same.</li>
<li>In 2012 he received a double-neck replica of the Red Special with the second neck having 12-strings. He used this guitar at a few gigs with <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> now being able to play the 12-string part from the studio version of Under Pressure live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Double-neck_Red_Special_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Double-neck_Red_Special-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>He currently has a Guild 12-string to replace his Ovation Pacemaker. Some of the non-RS electric guitars he used in the studio included:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burns_London" title="Burns London">Burns</a> Double Six on "Long Away" (1976) and "Under Pressure" (1981).</li>
<li>Fender Telecaster on "Crazy Little Thing Called Love" (1979). It was used for the video (but not the recordings) of "Back Chat" (1982).</li>
<li>Gibson Firebird on "Hammer to Fall" and "Tear It Up" (album versions only, not on stage).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ibanez_JS_Series" title="Ibanez JS Series">Ibanez JS</a> on "Nothing But Blue" (1991).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Parker_Fly" title="Parker Fly">Parker Fly</a> on "Mother Love" (1993–1995).</li>
</ul>
<p>For acoustic, he favoured Ovation, Martin, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkai_Guitars" title="Tōkai Guitars">Tōkai</a> Hummingbird, Godin and Guild. On a couple of videos he also used some different electric guitars: a Stratocaster copy on "Play the Game" (1980) and a <a href="/wiki/Washburn_RR-V_Tour_Series" title="Washburn RR-V Tour Series">Washburn RR2V</a> on "Princes of the Universe" (1986).</p>
<p>In 1984 <a href="/wiki/Guild_Guitar_Company" title="Guild Guitar Company">Guild</a> released the first official Red Special replica for mass production, and made some prototypes specifically for May. However the solid body construction (the original RS has hollow cavities in the body) and the pick-ups (DiMarzio) that were not an exact replica of the Burns TriSonic did not make May happy, so the production stopped after just 300 guitars. In 1993 Guild made a second replica of the RS, made in just 1000 copies, of which May has some and used as a back-up. At the moment, he uses the two guitars made by Greg Fryer—the luthier who restored the Old Lady in 1998—as back-up. They are almost identical to the original, except for the Fryer logo on the headstock (May's original one has a sixpence).</p>
<p>In the studio, May used <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_DX7" title="Yamaha DX7">Yamaha DX7</a> synths for the opening sequence of "<a href="/wiki/One_Vision" title="One Vision">One Vision</a>" and the backgrounds of "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" (also on stage), "<a href="/wiki/Scandal_(song)" title="Scandal (song)">Scandal</a>" and <a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">"The Show Must Go On"</a>. He mostly used Freddie Mercury's 1972 Steinway piano and reportedly now owns the instrument in question. May was keen on using some toys as instruments as well. He used a <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_Corporation" title="Yamaha Corporation">Yamaha</a> plastic piano in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teo_Torriatte" title="Teo Torriatte">Teo Torriatte</a>" and a toy mini <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koto_(musical_instrument)" title="Koto (musical instrument)">koto</a> in <a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">"The Prophet's Song"</a>. He also used a "genuine George Formby Ukulele-Banjo" in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bring_Back_That_Leroy_Brown" title="Bring Back That Leroy Brown">Bring Back That Leroy Brown</a>" and <a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">"Good Company"</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Amplifiers_and_effects">Amplifiers and effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Amplifiers and effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>May has used <a href="/wiki/Vox_AC30" title="Vox AC30">Vox AC30</a> amplifiers almost exclusively since a meeting with his long-time hero <a href="/wiki/Rory_Gallagher" title="Rory Gallagher">Rory Gallagher</a> at a gig in London during the late 1960s/early 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> In the mid-1970s he used six of them, with an <a href="/wiki/Echoplex" title="Echoplex">Echoplex</a> delay (with extended delay time) plugged into a separate amplifier, and a second Echoplex plugged into yet another amp; he used a homemade booster, his only effects pedal, which was on all the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reply_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-reply-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> His choice is the model AC30TBX, the top-boost version with Blue Alnico speakers, and he runs the amp at full volume on the Normal channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> He also customises his amps by removing the circuitry for the Brilliant and Vib-trem channels (leaving only the circuitry for the Normal), and this alters the tone slightly, with a gain addition of 6–7 dB. He always used a <a href="/wiki/Treble_booster" title="Treble booster">treble booster</a> which, along with the AC30 and his custom '<a href="/wiki/Deacy_Amp" title="Deacy Amp">Deacy Amp</a>' transistor amp, was built by Queen bass player John Deacon, went a long way in helping to create many of his signature guitar tones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> He used the Dallas Rangemaster for the first Queen albums, up to <i><a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_(album)" title="A Day at the Races (album)">A Day at the Races</a></i>. Effects guru <a href="/wiki/Pete_Cornish" title="Pete Cornish">Pete Cornish</a> built for him the TB-83 (32 dB of gain) that was used for all the remaining Queen albums. He switched in 2000 to the Fryer's booster, which actually gives less boost than the TB-83.</p>
<p>When performing live, he uses banks of Vox AC30 amplifiers keeping some amps with only guitar and others with all effects such as delay, flanger and chorus. He has a rack of 14 AC30s, which are grouped as Normal, Chorus, Delay 1, Delay 2. On his pedal board, May has a custom switch unit made by Cornish and subsequently modified by Fryer that allows him to choose which amps are active. He uses a <a href="/wiki/Boss_Corporation" title="Boss Corporation">BOSS</a> pedal from the '70s, the Chorus Ensemble CE-1, which can be heard in "<a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack" title="Sheer Heart Attack">In The Lap of The Gods</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Wembley_%2786" title="Live at Wembley '86">Live at Wembley '86</a></i>) or "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>" (slow version played live with P. Rodgers). Next in the chain, he uses a Foxx Foot Phaser ("We Will Rock You", "We Are the Champions", "Keep Yourself Alive", etc.), and two delay machines to play his trademark solo in "Brighton Rock".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1073" data-file-width="750" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg/220px-Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg/330px-Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg/440px-Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brian May in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1974 to 1988, May was married to Chrissie Mullen, who is the mother of his three offspring: Jimmy, born on 15 June 1978; Louisa, born on 22 May 1981 and Emily Ruth, born on 18 February 1987. May and Chrissie separated in 1988.
