Their separation and eventual divorce was publicised by British tabloid newspapers following reports that he had an affair with <i><a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a></i> actress <a href="/wiki/Anita_Dobson" title="Anita Dobson">Anita Dobson</a>, whom he met in 1986, and who gained fame in the 1980s as <a href="/wiki/Angie_Watts" title="Angie Watts">Angie Watts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> After a concert at Wembley Stadium, she inspired him to write the 1989 hit "I Want It All". They married on 18 November 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He has stated in interviews that he suffered from severe depression in the late 1980s and early 1990s, to the point of contemplating suicide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> for reasons having to do with his troubled first marriage, his perceived failure as a husband and a father, his father Harold's death and Freddie Mercury's illness and death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>May's father Harold worked as a <a href="/wiki/Drafter" title="Drafter">draughtsman</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Aviation" title="Ministry of Aviation">Ministry of Aviation</a> and was a long-time heavy cigarette smoker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, May dislikes smoking,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> even to the point where he has prohibited smoking indoors at his more recent concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> His father was disappointed that he abandoned his scientific education to become a rock musician, but after May flew both his parents to New York to attend Queen's first concert in <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>, his father said that he "got it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dm25apr10_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-dm25apr10-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times_(UK)" title="The Sunday Times (UK)">The Sunday Times</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Rich List</a> he is worth £85 million or around $135 million as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Brian May is a vegetarian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Astrophysics">Astrophysics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Astrophysics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>May studied physics and mathematics at <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, graduating with a BSc (Hons) degree and <a href="/wiki/Associate_of_the_Royal_College_of_Science" title="Associate of the Royal College of Science">ARCS</a> in physics with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second-class_honours" title="Second-class honours">Upper Second-Class Honours</a>. From 1970 to 1974, he studied for a PhD degree at Imperial College, studying reflected light from interplanetary dust and the velocity of dust in the plane of the Solar System. When Queen started to have international success in 1974, he abandoned his doctoral studies, but co-authored two scientific research papers: <i>MgI Emission in the Night-Sky Spectrum</i> (1972)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>An Investigation of the Motion of <a href="/wiki/Zodiacal_light" title="Zodiacal light">zodiacal dust</a> Particles (Part I)</i> (1973),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> which were based on his observations at the <a href="/wiki/Teide_Observatory" title="Teide Observatory">Teide Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>.</p>
<p>In October 2006, May re-registered for his PhD at Imperial College and submitted his thesis in August 2007 (one year earlier than he estimated it would take to complete). As well as writing up the previous work he had done, May had to review the work on zodiacal dust undertaken during the intervening 33 years, which included the discovery of the zodiacal dust bands by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/IRAS" title="IRAS">IRAS</a> satellite. After a viva voce, the revised thesis (entitled <i>A Survey of Radial Velocities in the Zodiacal Dust Cloud</i>) was approved in September 2007, some 37 years after it had been commenced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buzzcocksphd_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-buzzcocksphd-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> He was able to submit his thesis only because of the minimal amount of research on the topic during the intervening years and has described the subject as one that became "trendy" again in the 2000s. He graduated at the awards ceremony of Imperial College held in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> on 14 May 2008.</p>
<p>In October 2007, May was appointed a Visiting Researcher in Imperial College and continues his interest in astronomy and involvement with the Imperial Astrophysics Group.</p>
<p>He is co-author, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Patrick_Moore" title="Sir Patrick Moore">Sir Patrick Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Lintott" title="Chris Lintott">Chris Lintott</a>, of <i>Bang! – The Complete History of the Universe</i> (published in 2006)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and "The Cosmic Tourist" (published in 2012).</p>
<p>Asteroid <a href="/wiki/52665_Brianmay" title="52665 Brianmay">52665 Brianmay</a> was named in his honour on 18 June 2008 on the suggestion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Patrick_Moore" title="Sir Patrick Moore">Sir Patrick Moore</a> (probably influenced by the asteroid's provisional designation of <span class="nowrap">1998 <b>BM</b><sub>30</sub></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rdspecial_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-rdspecial-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>May appeared on the 700th episode of <a href="/wiki/The_Sky_at_Night" title="The Sky at Night">The Sky at Night</a> hosted by Sir Patrick Moore, along with Chris Lintott, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Culshaw" title="Jon Culshaw">Jon Culshaw</a>, Prof. <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cox_(physicist)" title="Brian Cox (physicist)">Brian Cox</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Astronomer_Royal" title="Astronomer Royal">Astronomer Royal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Rees" title="Martin Rees">Martin Rees</a> who on departing the panel, told Brian May, who was joining it, "I don't know a scientist who looks as much like <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> as you do".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> May was also a guest on the first episode of the third series of the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Stargazing_Live" title="Stargazing Live">Stargazing Live</a></i>, on 8 January 2013.</p>
<p>On 17 November 2007, May was appointed Chancellor of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_John_Moores_University" title="Liverpool John Moores University">Liverpool John Moores University</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Chancellor_confirmed_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Chancellor_confirmed-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> taking over from <a href="/wiki/Cherie_Blair" title="Cherie Blair">Cherie Blair</a>, and installed in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May_installed_as_uni_chancellor_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-May_installed_as_uni_chancellor-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> He held the post until 2013.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activism">Activism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Activism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Badger_culling_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Badger culling in the United Kingdom">Badger culling in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="347" data-file-width="317" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg/220px-Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f3/Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f3/Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May filming for the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s <i>The One Show</i> in 2011 for an anti badger culling campaign.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brian May has formed a group to promote animal welfare. Though a <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> voter most of his life,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> he has stated that their policies on <a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">fox hunting</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Culling" title="Culling">culling</a> of <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badgers</a> meant he did not vote for them at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 General Election</a>. His group, <a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(animal_welfare)" title="Save Me (animal welfare)">Save Me</a> (named after <a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">the May-written Queen song</a>), campaigns for the protection of all animals against unnecessary, cruel and degrading treatment; with a particular emphasis on preventing hunting of foxes and the culling of badgers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The group's primary concern is to ensure that the <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Act_2004" title="Hunting Act 2004">Hunting Act 2004</a> and other laws protecting animals are retained in situ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-save-me.org.uk_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-save-me.org.uk-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview in September 2010 with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sackur" title="Stephen Sackur">Stephen Sackur</a> for the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/HARDtalk" title="HARDtalk">HARDtalk</a></i> program, May said that he would rather be remembered for his animal rights work than for his music or scientific work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> May is a staunch supporter of the RSPCA, the International Fund For Animal Welfare, the League Against Cruel Sports, PETA UK and the Harper Asprey Wildlife Rescue.</p>
<p>In March 2012, May contributed the foreword to a target paper published by the think tank the <a href="/wiki/Bow_Group" title="Bow Group">Bow Group</a>, urging the government to reconsider its plans to cull thousands of badgers to control bovine TB, stating that the findings of Labour's major badger culling trials, several years earlier, show that culling does not work. The paper was authored by Graham Godwin-Pearson with contributions by leading <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> scientists, including <a href="/wiki/John_Krebs,_Baron_Krebs" title="John Krebs, Baron Krebs">Lord Krebs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Brian May joined French guitar player <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Danel" title="Jean-Pierre Danel">Jean-Pierre Danel</a> for a charity Danel launched to the benefit of animal rights in France. The guitarists signed guitars and art photos together, and were joined by <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2013, May teamed up with actor <a href="/wiki/Brian_Blessed" title="Brian Blessed">Brian Blessed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flash_animation" title="Flash animation">Flash</a> cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Jonti_Picking" title="Jonti Picking">Jonti "Weebl" Picking</a>, as well as animal rights groups including the RSPCA, to form "Team Badger", a "coalition of organisations that have teamed up to fight the planned cull of badgers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> With Weebl and Blessed, May recorded a single, <i><a href="/wiki/Save_The_Badger_Badger_Badger" title="Save The Badger Badger Badger">Save The Badger Badger Badger</a></i> – a <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mashup</a> of Weebl's viral 2003 Flash cartoon <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">meme</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badger_Badger_Badger" title="Badger Badger Badger">Badger Badger Badger</a></i>, and Queen's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_(song)" title="Flash (song)">Flash</a></i>, featuring vocals by Blessed. Weebl animated <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EllYgcWmcAY" rel="nofollow">the music video</a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, parodying both Weebl's <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EIyixC9NsLI" rel="nofollow">original animation</a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> and a scene from <i><a href="/wiki/Flash_Gordon_(film)" title="Flash Gordon (film)">Flash Gordon</a></i>, a film featuring music by Queen, and in which Blessed played Prince Vultan. On 1 September 2013, <i>Save The Badger Badger Badger</i> charted at No. 79 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>, No. 39 on the UK <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> chart<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalspy_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspy-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> and No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> Rock chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stereophotography">Stereophotography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Stereophotography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>May has had a lifelong interest in collecting Victorian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stereophotography" title="Stereophotography">stereophotography</a>. In 2009, with co-author Elena Vidal, he published his second book, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Village_Lost_and_Found" title="A Village Lost and Found">A Village Lost and Found</a>,</i> on the work of English stereophotography innovator <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Richard_Williams" title="Thomas Richard Williams">T. R. Williams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> He was awarded The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Photographic_Society" title="Royal Photographic Society">Royal Photographic Society</a>'s Saxby Medal in 2012 for achievement in the field of three-dimensional imaging.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>May made a significant technical contribution to the book to accompany the exhibition 'Stereoscopic Photographs of Pablo Picasso by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mouzillat" title="Robert Mouzillat">Robert Mouzillat</a>' held at the Holburne Museum in Bath, UK from February 2014 to June 2014. The book provides a cross-section of photographs of Picasso in his studio, at the bullfight at Arles and in his garden. May's 3D 'Owl viewer' is used to view the photographs in 3D.</p>
<p>The purchase of his first card in 1973 started May on a lifelong and world-wide search for <a href="/wiki/Les_Diableries" title="Les Diableries">Les Diableries</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> which are stereoscopic photographs depicting scenes of daily life in Hell. On 10 October 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> the book 'Diableries: Stereoscopic Adventures in Hell' by Brian May, Denis Pellerin and Paula Fleming was published.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
